wewa 6(1) I 8(1)(P)

The impugned construction is outside the radius of 250 metres of Hussaini Dalan, though the respondent nos. 6 and 13 knew very well that the same is well therewithin from Hussaini Dalan. In the facts and circumstances of the case, we are of the opinion that this ticking of ÓbvÓ was done deliberately in order to obtain the Land Use Certificate from RAJUK without any hitch. The consequence of furnishing any erroneous or misleading information in the prescribed Land Use Certificate Form is that it will automatically lead to the cancellation of the Land Use Certificate itself in accordance with its clause 5. What we are driving at boils down to this: the Land Use Certificate granted by the respondent no. 1 (RAJUK) in favour of the respondent nos. 6 and 13 has stood cancelled automatically because of the deliberately supplied misleading information in the Land Use Certificate Form. No further order is required from RAJUK for cancellation of this Land Use Certificate. . . . (40)

Building Construction Act, 1952

Sections 3 and 9

Because of the deliberate supply of the wrong information in the Land Use Certificate Form adverted to above, the Special Project Certificate has stood cancelled automatically too. In this regard as well, no further order of cancellation of the Special Project Certificate is required from RAJUK. For intentionally furnishing the wrong information by the respondent nos. 6 and 13 as above, the sanctions granted by RAJUK in respect of the impugned construction on the case property cannot be maintained at all pursuant to section 9 of the Act of 1952.         . . . Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972

Article 102

The respondent nos. 6 and 13 will have to apply to RAJUK afresh for a Land Use Certificate and a Special Project Certificate for the impugned construction on the case property. If those respondents file applications to RAJUK afresh to the above effect, then RAJUK will review the entire gamut of the issues involved and consider their pros and cons and arrive at a correct decision as to granting or non-granting of any Land Use Certificate and Special Project Certificate in the light of the relevant laws.    . . . JUDGMENT

Moyeenul Islam Chowdhury, J:  On an application under article 102 of the Constitution of the People’s Republic of Bangladesh filed by the petitioner, a Rule Nisi was issued calling upon the respondents to show cause as to why the permission of the respondent no. 1 (RAJUK) for the construction of a 12 (twelve)-storied building by the respondent no. 13 on C.S Plot No. 107 under Holding No. 29, Hussaini Dalan Road, Lalbagh, Dhaka which is adjacent to the petitioner’s premises (Hussaini Dalan) should not be declared to be without lawful authority and of no legal effect and why the respondent no. 1 should not be directed to cancel the Land Use Certificate (i¥¢j hÉhq¡l R¡sfœ) given to the respondent nos. 2-12 and/or 13 in connection with the construction of the aforesaid 12 (twelve)-storied building and/or such other or further order or orders passed as to this Court may seem fit and proper.

2.             The case of the petitioner, as set out in the Writ Petition, in short, is as follows:

The petitioner is Hussaini Dalan Imambara Waqf Estate represented by its Superintendent. This Hussaini Dalan Imambara Waqf Estate is situated on Holding No. 30, Hussaini Dalan Road under Police Station Lalbagh, District- Dhaka comprising C. S. Plot Nos. 104 and 105 and enrolled with the office of the Administrator of Waqfs being E. C. No. 11737.  Rajdhani Unnayan Kartipakkha (RAJUK) by a Gazette Notification No. l¡SEL/ f¢lx(Ex¢ex)/1-Hj-220/07/fËn¡x/185Øq¡x dated 02.02.2009, pursuant to Rule 61 of Y¡L¡ jq¡eNl Cj¡la (¢ejÑ¡Z, Eæue, pwlrZ J Afp¡lZ) ¢h¢dj¡m¡, 2008 (hereinafter referred to as the Rules of 2008), declared Hussaini Dalan as a historical/heritage establishment. The respondent no. 13 is constructing a building on C. S. Plot No. 107 under Holding No. 29, Hussaini Dalan Road, Lalbagh, Dhaka (impugned construction) which is adjacent to Hussaini Dalan. The impugned construction is being allowed by RAJUK in violation of the provisions of article 24 of the Constitution of the People’s Republic of Bangladesh, the Rules of 2008 read with the Antiquities Act, 1968. As per Rule 61(M) of the Rules of 2008, for conservation and preservation of any listed heritage site, RAJUK is required to consult with the Department of Archaeology, Government of Bangladesh, the Institute of Architects, Bangladesh or with those who are experts in buildings which are aesthetically, historically, scientifically, socially or spiritually important. RAJUK requested the Department of Archaeology vide Memo No. 25.39.0000.049.38.100.15.89(1) Øq¡x dated 03.03.2016 to evaluate the distance of the proposed building under the impugned construction on C. S. Plot No. 107 from Hussaini Dalan. The Department of Archaeology by its Memo No. 43.23.2600.128.18.11.15/525 dated 28.04.2016 replied to RAJUK’s Memo dated 03.03.2016 stating that “®q¡pe£ c¡m¡e q­a fËÙ¹¡¢ha ih­el c§laÄ ¢eZÑ­ul SeÉ fËaÁašÆ A¢dcçl La«ÑL N¢Wa Cj¡la ¢ejÑ¡Z R¡sfœ ¢houL L¢j¢Vl ja¡ja pwk¤š² Ll¡ q­m¡z fËÙ¹¡¢ha ihe¢V ®q¡pe£ c¡m¡­el 250 ¢jV¡­ll j­dÉ Ah¢Øqa qJu¡u ihe j¡¢mL­L 1.5 ¢jV¡l Ae¤i¨¢jL Øq¡e R¡s­a q­h Hhw ®q¢l­V­Sl e¡¾c¢eL ®~h¢nÖVÉ hS¡u l¡M¡l SeÉ p¤EµQ ihe ¢ejÑ¡Z e¡ Ll¡l ¢ho­u ja¡ja fËc¡e Ll¡ q­u­R”. The opinion of the Building Construction Clearance Committee of the Department of Archaeology was also communicated to RAJUK as an attachment to the Department of Archaeology Memo where the aforesaid Clearance Committee expressed that “fËÙ¹¡¢ha ihe¢V ®q¡pe£ c¡m¡­el p£j¡e¡l 250 ¢jV¡­ll j­dÉ Ah¢Øqa qJu¡u A¡e¤i¨¢jLi¡­h 1.50 ¢jV¡l S¡uN¡ ®R­s ea¥e ihe ¢ejÑ¡Z Ll¡ ®k­a f¡­l Hhw ®q¡pe£ c¡m¡­el cª¢ÖVe¡¾c¢eLa¡­L Ar¥ZÀ l¡M¡l SeÉ S¡q¡‰£leNl ¢hnÄ¢hcÉ¡m­ul pq­k¡N£ AdÉ¡fL j¡¢mq¡ e¡¢NÑp p­hÑ¡µQ ¢ae am¡ fkÑ¿¹ ihe¢V ¢ejÑ¡Z Ll¡ ®k­a f¡­l j­jÑ ja fËL¡n L­lez L¢j¢Vl AeÉ¡eÉ pcpÉNZ p¤EµQ ihe ¢ejÑ¡Z e¡ Ll¡l ¢ho­u HLja ®f¡oZ L­le”. However, the petitioner by its letters dated 20.06.2017 informed the Chairman and the Chief Town Planner of RAJUK that the respondent nos. 2-12 had been acting in contravention of the relevant laws by constructing the building adjacent to the boundary of Hussaini Dalan and the impugned construction would deface and restrict the aesthetic beauty of Hussaini Dalan. In reply, RAJUK by its Memo No. 25.39.0000.030. 99.028.17-1028 dated 20.11.2017 stated, amongst others, that a Land Use Certificate had already been given subject to the acceptance of the opinion of the Department of Archaeology. As the Land Use Certificate of RAJUK was given with reference to the case property, that is to say, Plot No. 107 under Holding No. 29, Hussaini Dalan Road, Lalbagh, Dhaka in violation of the relevant provisions of the Rules of 2008 and the Antiquities Act, 1968, the petitioner filed the Writ Petition and obtained the instant Rule.

3.             In the Supplementary Affidavit dated 11.07.2018 filed on behalf of the petitioner, it has been stated that the petitioner filed the Writ Petition through the Superintendent of Hussaini Dalan and the Superintendent was authorized to file the Writ Petition as evidenced by Annexure- ‘K’ series to the Supplementary Affidavit.

4.             The respondent nos. 1, 6 and 13 have contested the Rule by filing separate Affidavits-in-Opposition. Their case, in brief, runs as follows:

5.             The respondent no. 13, that is to say, Image Properties Limited is not constructing a 12-storied building on the case property; rather it is constructing a 9-storied building along with one basement thereon in compliance with the terms and conditions of the Special Project Certificate dated 01.11.2016 and the approved construction plan dated 17.01.2017. In fact, the respondent no. 13, in compliance with the relevant rules and procedure, obtained the Land Use Certificate, Special Project Certificate and approval of the construction plan of the respondent no. 6 from RAJUK. The respondent no. 1 accorded permission to the other respondents to construct the proposed building on the case property in accordance with law. The respondent nos. 2, 3, 4, 5, 9, 10 and 11 died long ago and the respondent nos. 6, 7 and 8 are the owners-in-possession of the case property. Those respondent nos. 6, 7 and 8 appointed the respondent no. 13 as their attorney to construct a 9-storied building along with one basement thereon. Since the case property is situated adjacent to Hussaini Dalan, the respondent no. 1 sought opinion from the Department of Archaeology with regard to the approval of the Land Use Certificate. Accordingly the concerned authority of the Department of Archaeology conducted an inquiry and forwarded the inquiry report to the Director General, Department of Archaeology by its Memo No. 43.23.2600.128.33.10.11.902 dated 20.08.2014. Thereafter the Director General of the Department of Archaeology, on the basis of the inquiry report, issued a no-objection certificate vide Memo No. fËaÁx/l¡SEL /3M/4/06/Awn-3/2210(2) dated 28.08.2014. Against this backdrop, the respondent no. 1 issued the Land Use Certificate dated 18.09.2014 in favour of the other respondents.

6.             At one stage, the respondent no. 1 requested the Regional Director, Department of Archaeology to determine the distance of the case property from Hussaini Dalan on 03.03.2016. Thereafter the relevant authority of the Department of Archaeology made a report on 24.04.2016. One of the Members of the Committee concerned opined that a 3-storied building might be constructed and other Members of the Committee opined not to construct any high-rise building thereon. However, the Director General of the Department of Archaeology forwarded the report to the respondent no. 1 by Memo No. 43.23.2600.128.18.11.15/525 dated 28.04.2016 recommending not to construct any high-rise building on the case property as the same is situated within a radius of 250 metres from Hussaini Dalan. The Secretary of the Special Committee of RAJUK wrote a letter to the Regional Director, Department of Archaeology on 20.07.2016 contending that since the proposed building is not a high-rise one under section 2(63) of the Building Construction Act, 1952, the construction of the building requires permission. The Director General, Department of Archaeology replied to the respondent no. 1 (RAJUK) on 22.08.2016 not to construct any high-rise building on the case property. Anyway, after observing all legal formalities, the respondent no. 1 approved the Special Project Certificate on 01.11.2016. On 17.01.2017, RAJUK approved the construction plan of the respondent no. 6 for the 9-storied building along with one basement. But the petitioner practised fraud upon the Court by stating that the respondents were constructing a 12-storied building on the case property and obtained the Rule Nisi along with an interim order of injunction. As the attorney of the respondent no. 6, the respondent no. 13 already took over possession of the case property and completed the earth work of the basement and was going to start the actual construction work. But because of the interim order of injunction passed by this Court, the construction work was stopped. The only grievance of the petitioner is that if the respondents construct the proposed building, the beauty of Hussaini Dalan will be affected. But the Department of Archaeology and RAJUK opined that the distance between Hussaini Dalan and the case property is 220 feet and there is no possibility of disfigurement of Hussaini Dalan.

7.             In the Affidavit-in-Reply dated 29.05.2018 filed on behalf of the petitioner, it has been averred that the petitioner, not being an expert in the building construction, genuinely believed that 10 stories plus 2 stories for basement (car park) totalling 12 stories were being built by the respondent no. 13. The petitioner was unaware of the fact that the respondent nos. 2, 3, 4, 5, 9, 10 and 11 were dead. The impugned construction is only 220 feet from Hussaini Dalan. So any development work within a radius of 250 metres from Hussaini Dalan requires conforming to the provisions of Rule 61 of the Rules of 2008. The preservation of the aesthetic beauty of Hussaini Dalan falls within the ambit of the aforesaid Rule 61.    

8.             At the outset, Mr. Junayed Ahmed Chowdhury, learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the petitioner, submits that indisputably the impugned construction of the 9-storied building is being raised on the case property which is adjacent to the boundary wall of Hussaini Dalan and the distance between Hussaini Dalan and the case property is 220 feet and the opinion of the Department of Archaeology given pursuant to Rule 61(kha) of the Rules of 2008 clearly shows that the building should not be more than 3-storied keeping in mind the aesthetic importance of Hussaini Dalan and despite such recommendation, RAJUK issued the Land Use Certificate by its Memo No. 25.39.0000.030.99. 028.17-1028 dated 20.11.2017 for the 12-storied building without any explanation whatsoever.

9.             Mr. Junayed Ahmed Chowdhury also submits that under Rule 9(2) of the Rules of 2008, RAJUK is required to disclose the drawings of the impugned construction for public observation and comments and to take public opinion including that of the petitioner for a period of 15(fifteen) days before issuance of the Land Use Certificate; but unfortunately the petitioner was not consulted before RAJUK allowed the impugned construction to proceed.

10.         Mr. Junayed Ahmed Chowdhury further submits that assuming for the sake of argument that RAJUK does not have any obligation to consult the petitioner under the Rules of 2008, in that event, RAJUK has a common-law duty to consult the petitioner to ensure fairness, especially when Hussaini Dalan is the next door neighbour of the respondent no. 6 and the impugned construction would clearly have an impact on its aesthetic appearance as evidenced by the opinion rendered by the Department of Archaeology.

11.         Mr. Junayed Ahmed Chowdhury next submits that while allowing the impugned construction to proceed on the case property, RAJUK ought to have taken into consideration that public interest lies in protection and preservation of heritage/establishment sites as mandated by article 24 of the Constitution and there has to be an application of mind on issues linked with preservation of historical sites like Hussaini Dalan and by issuing the Land Use Certificate for the 12-storied building in total disregard of the recommendation given by the Department of Archaeology, RAJUK exhibited a complete lack of sensitivity towards the duty of preservation of Hussaini Dalan.

12.         Mr. Junayed Ahmed Chowdhury also submits that the citizens have a right to protection from the threats of man-made hazards and the State is bound to protect the health and longevity of its people and the right to life includes the citizens’ freedom from violence, but RAJUK allowed the impugned construction on the case property ignoring a valid security issue in view of the fact that on 26.10.2015 due to terrorist bomb blasts in Hussaini Dalan, fatalities and injuries occurred.

13.         Mr. Junayed Ahmed Chowdhury further submits that admittedly the petitioner is the Hussaini Dalan Imambara Waqf Estate which is being represented by its Superintendent and the Superintendent of Hussaini Dalan has been authorized by its Managing Committee as evidenced by Annexure- ‘K’ series to file and/or defend any case in any Court of law and considered from this vantage point, the Writ Petition is maintainable.

14.         Mr. Junayed Ahmed Chowdhury next submits that as the petitioner is not an expert in building construction and engineering matters, it genuinely believed that the respondent nos. 6 and 13 were raising a 12-storied building on the case property and accordingly he has made a statement in that regard in the Writ Petition and this genuine mistake can not be construed as a fraud practised upon the Court at the time of issuance of the Rule Nisi along with the interim order of injunction.

15.         Mr. Junayed Ahmed Chowdhury further submits that shockingly enough, the respondent nos. 6 and 13 suppressed material facts and resorted to fraud in filling up the prescribed Form-101 (Land Use Certificate Application Form) under Rule 4(3) and under Rule 6(1) of the Rules of 2008, the City Planning Division of RAJUK approved and issued the Land Use Certificate in their favour under certain terms and conditions.

16.         Mr. Junayed Ahmed Chowdhury also submits that an applicant has to disclose certain information in the Land Use Certificate Application Form and clause  6(R) thereof requires the applicant to disclose whether the land in question is within a radius of 250 metres from any historical monument, that is to say, from Hussaini Dalan in this case and the respondent nos. 6 and 13 ticked “e¡” which misled RAJUK into believing that the impugned construction is outside the radius of 250 metres from Hussaini Dalan and this intentional perpetration of fraud on their part prompted RAJUK in issuing the Land Use Certificate; but nevertheless the said certificate stood cancelled automatically in view of its clause 5.

17.         Mr. Junayed Ahmed Chowdhury further submits that for the self-same perpetration of fraud, the Special Project Certificate issued by RAJUK in favour of the respondent nos. 6 and 13 under Rule 8(1)(Q) of the Rules of 2008 also stood cancelled as a matter of course by reason of its clause 4.

18.         Mr. Junayed Ahmed Chowdhury next submits that regard being had to the Rules of 2008 and the Antiquities Act, 1968, RAJUK should not have provided the respondent nos. 6 and 13 with any Land Use Certificate and Special Project Certificate for the impugned construction on the case property and given this scenario, the Rule ought to be made absolute.

19.         Per contra, Mr. Md. Nurul Amin, learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the respondent nos. 6 and 13, submits that admittedly the distance between Hussaini Dalan and the case property is 220 feet and there are many multi-storied and high-rise buildings in the vicinity of Hussaini Dalan within a radius of 250 metres and in that view of the matter, the respondent no. 1 (RAJUK) lawfully granted the Land Use Certificate and the Special Project Certificate in favour of the respondent nos. 6 and 13 as per the Rules of 2008.

20.         Mr. Md. Nurul Amin also submits that prior to granting the Land Use Certificate and the Special Project Certificate, RAJUK attached due importance to the opinion given by the Department of Archaeology and as such it can not be said at all that the opinion of the Department of Archaeology was set at naught while issuing the same by RAJUK.

21.         Mr. Md. Nurul Amin next submits that as the distance between the case property and Hussaini Dalan is 220 feet, there is no question of disfigurement of Hussaini Dalan as contemplated by article 24 of the Constitution.

22.         Mr. Md. Nurul Amin further submits that at the time of constructing various multi-storied and high-rise buildings in the vicinity of Hussaini Dalan, the petitioner did not raise any objection whatsoever and given this situation, the principles of estoppel, waiver and acquiescence have come into play in this case and that being so, the Rule should be discharged.

23.         Mr. Md. Nurul Amin also submits that there is a signboard hung on the case property in front of the impugned construction and it has been clearly and conspicuously written in the signboard that the impugned construction is a 9-storied building with one basement and as the signboard is visible and within the knowledge of the petitioner, it does not stand to reason and logic as to why the petitioner has laid a claim in the Writ Petition that the respondent nos. 6 and 13 are raising a 12-storied building on the case property.

24.         Mr. Md. Nurul Amin next submits that the assertion that the respondent nos. 6 and 13 are raising a 12-storied building on the case property was calculated to mislead the Court and by misleading the Court and resorting to fraud, the petitioner obtained the Rule Nisi along with the interim order of injunction and this phenomenon bears ample testimony that the petitioner did not invoke the writ jurisdiction of the High Court Division under article 102 of the Constitution with clean hands and on this count alone, the Rule should be discharged.

25.         Mr. Md. Nurul Amin further submits that it is true that in the prescribed Land Use Certificate Form, the respondent nos. 6 and 13 ticked “e¡” against clause 6(R) which runs– “fÓ­Vl 250 ¢jV¡l c§l­aÄl j­dÉ AhØq¡ex I¢aq¡¢pL …l¦aÄf§ZÑ p¡CV (qyÉ¡/e¡)” and as the respondent no. 6 is an ordinary person, he could not understand the import of this clause 6(R) and because of this bona fide mistake, the Land Use Certificate and the Special Project Certificate granted by RAJUK in favour of the respondent nos. 6 and 13 can not be thrown to the winds.

26.         Mr. Md. Nurul Amin next submits that regard being had to the facts and circumstances of the case, the Rule Nisi issued in this Writ Petition should be discharged with costs.

27.         Mr. Md. Hefzul Bari, learned Advocate appearing for the respondent no. 1, adopts the submissions advanced by Mr. Md. Nurul Amin.

28.         We have heard the submissions of the learned Advocate Mr. Junayed Ahmed Chowdhury and the counter-submissions of the learned Advocate Mr. Md. Nurul Amin and perused the Writ Petition, Supplementary Affidavit, Affidavits-in-Opposition, Affidavit-in-Reply and relevant Annexures annexed thereto.

29.         There is no gainsaying the fact that the respondent no. 1 (RAJUK) has acknowledged Hussaini Dalan as a historical establishment. It is also admitted that the 9-storied building on the case property is being raised at a distance of 220 feet from Hussaini Dalan. Undeniably there are many multi-storied and high-rise buildings within a radius of 250 metres from Hussaini Dalan. It is also undisputed that the petitioner does not lay any claim to the case property. The petitioner is only interested in ensuring the aesthetic beauty of Hussaini Dalan.

30.         Anyway, the petitioner has made a categorical statement on oath that the respondent nos. 6 and 13 are constructing a 12-storied building on the case property, that is to say, on C. S. Plot No. 107 under Holding No. 29, Hussaini Dalan Road, Lalbagh, Dhaka. It transpires that there is a signboard hung on the case property in front of the impugned construction. The petitioner is represented by its Superintendent who is also the Member-Secretary of its Managing Committee. In the natural course of things, a man of ordinary prudence is set to take notice of the signboard and read the writings thereon. We are unable to understand as to why the Superintendent of Hussaini Dalan failed to take notice of the signboard and the fact that a 9-storied building is being constructed on the case property. The Superintendent of Hussaini Dalan is an educated person. He is not Tom, Dick and Harry. He is not a man in the street.

31.         Before making any statement on oath before this Court, the Superintendent of Hussaini Dalan should have been very careful and circumspect. Had he been so, he would have instructed his lawyer that a 9-storied (instead of 12-storied) building is being erected on the case property. In this context, it is to be remembered that a statement made on oath before any Court of law has its sanctity and inviolability. Since the Superintendent has made a misleading statement in the Writ Petition with regard to the number of stories in the impugned construction, we strongly disapprove and deprecate his conduct in this respect.

32.         In order to be on the safe side, the petitioner could have filed an application to RAJUK under the relevant provisions of abÉ A¢dL¡l BCe, 2009 to know the exact nature of the impugned construction (inclusive of the number of stories) that is being raised on the case property. But the petitioner did not bother thereabout. It seems that the petitioner did not exercise due diligence in this regard.

33.         At this juncture, let us address the question of non-maintainability of the Writ Petition before this Court by the Superintendent of Hussaini Dalan as raised by Mr. Md. Nurul Amin. According to Mr. Md. Nurul Amin, the Superintendent was not authorized by any resolution of the Managing Committee of Hussaini Dalan to file the Writ Petition and on this score, he should be shown the door.

34.         Section 34(1) of the Waqfs Ordinance, 1962 provides that notwithstanding anything contained elsewhere in this Ordinance, or any other law for the time being in force, or in any decree or order of any court, or in any deed or instrument, the Administrator may, by notification in the official Gazette, take over and assume the administration, control, management and maintenance of any Waqf property including any shrine, dargah, imambara or other religious institution appertaining to such Waqf property. Again section 34(3) of the Waqfs Ordinance, 1962 postulates that  the Administrator may manage the Waqf property taken over by him under sub-section (1) through any officer subordinate to him or by an agent or official Mutawalli or, if he considers necessary, by appointing a Managing Committee in the case of a shrine, dargah, imambara or other religious institutions.

35.         In the present case before us, a Managing Committee of Hussaini Dalan is in place. As already observed, the Superintendent of Hussaini Dalan is the Member-Secretary of its Managing Committee. A reference to Annexure- ‘K’ series to the Supplementary Affidavit dated 11.07.2018 unerringly shows that there has been a Managing Committee of Hussaini Dalan Imambara Waqf Estate since 1959 and this Waqf Estate is being represented all through by its Superintendent. The incumbent Superintendent of Hussaini Dalan is Mr. M. M. Firoz Hossain. A conjoint reading of the aforesaid Annexure-‘K’ series lead us to hold that the incumbent Superintendent Mr. M. M. Firoz Hossain is amply authorized by the Managing Committee to file/institute or defend any case or other legal proceeding in any Court of law for and on behalf of Hussaini Dalan. In this perspective, Mr. M. M. Firoz Hossain has preferred the instant Writ Petition in the High Court Division under article 102 of the Constitution. So no objection can be raised to the maintainability of the Writ Petition before this Court. In the result, the contention of Mr. Md. Nurul Amin that the Writ Petition is not maintainable stands discarded.

36.         Rule 4(3) of the Rules of 2008 is as follows:

“4(3) S¢jl j¡¢mL¡e¡ pwœ²¡¿¹ L¡NSfœpq fÐÙ¹¡¢ha S¢j h¡ p¡CV hÉhq¡­ll ¢e¢jš i¨¢j hÉhq¡l R¡sf­œl SeÉ ¢ed¡Ñ¢la ¢g pq ¢ed¡Ñ¢la RL (glj-101) Hl j¡dÉ­j B­hce L¢l­a qC­hz”

37.         Again Rule 6(1) of the Rules of 2008 contemplates:

“6(1) i¨¢j hÉhq¡l R¡sf­œl B­hce c¡¢M­ml 30 (¢œn) ¢c­el j­dÉ La«Ñf­rl eNl f¢lLÒfe¡ n¡M¡ fÐ­u¡S­e ®k ®L¡e naÑ¡hm£ B­l¡f L¢lu¡ ¢edÑ¡¢la RL (glj-102) Hl j¡dÉ­j Ae¤­j¡ce fÐc¡e Abh¡ ¢m¢Ma L¡lZ fÐcnÑef§hÑL ¢edÑ¡¢la RL (glj-103) Hl j¡dÉ­j B­hce fÐaÉ¡M¡e L¢l­a f¡¢l­hz”

38.         Unquestionably the respondent nos. 6 and 13 applied to the respondent no. 1 (RAJUK) filling in the prescribed Form-101 under Rule 4(3) and RAJUK granted the Land Use Certificate in their favour under certain terms and conditions in the prescribed Form, that is to say, Form-102 under Rule 6(1) of the Rules of 2008.

39.         At this stage, it is important to note clause 5 of the Land Use Certificate which has been couched in the following terms:

“5z ­L¡e abÉ ®N¡fe L¢l­m h¡ i¤m abÉ fËc¡e L¢l­m fËc¡eL«a R¡sfœ h¡¢am h¢mu¡ NZÉ qC­hz”.

In this connection, we further note that an applicant has to disclose certain information in the prescribed Land Use Certificate Form. Clause 6(R) of the aforesaid prescribed Form requires the applicant to disclose whether the land in question is within a radius of 250 meters from any historical monument, that is to say, “fÔ­Vl 250 ¢jV¡l c§l­aÄl j­dÉ AhØq¡ex I¢aq¡¢pL …l¦aÄf§ZÑ p¡CV (qyÉ¡/e¡)”. It is admitted that in the prescribed Land Use Certificate Form, the respondents concerned ticked “e¡” meaning thereby that the proposed construction of the 9-storied building along with one basement is not within a radius of 250 meters from the historical establishment, that is to say, Hussaini Dalan.

40.         Now a pertinent question arises: what is the consequence of ticking “e¡” in clause 6(R) of the prescribed Land Use Certificate Form by the concerned respondents? This ticking of “e¡” was enough to mislead the respondent no. 1 (RAJUK) into believing that the impugned construction is outside the radius of 250 meters of Hussaini Dalan, though the respondent Nos. 6 and 13 knew very well that the same is well therewithin from Hussaini Dalan. In the facts and circumstances of the case, we are of the opinion that this ticking of “e¡” was done deliberately in order to obtain the Land Use Certificate from RAJUK without any hitch. The consequence of furnishing any erroneous or misleading information in the prescribed Land Use Certificate Form is that it will automatically lead to the cancellation of the Land Use Certificate itself in accordance with its clause 5. What we are driving at boils down to this: the Land Use Certificate granted by the respondent no. 1 (RAJUK) in favour of the respondent nos. 6 and 13 has stood cancelled automatically because of the deliberately supplied misleading information in the Land Use Certificate Form. No further order is required from RAJUK for cancellation of this Land Use Certificate.

41.         Furthermore, clause 4 of the Special Project Certificate issued by RAJUK in favour of the respondent nos. 6 and 13 under Rule 8(1)(Q) of the Rules of 2008 spells out that “R¡sf­œl ®k ®L¡e e£¢aj¡m¡ m´Oe, B­hcefœ, eLÚn¡ ¢Lwh¡ B­hceL¡l£ La«ÑL ®fnL«a AeÉ¡eÉ c¢mm CaÉ¡¢c­a E­ŸnÉj§mL i¡­h fËLªa a­bÉl i¥m EfØq¡fe h¡ ®N¡fe L¢l­m ¢h­no R¡sfœ h¡¢am h¢mu¡ NZÉ qC­hz” (Underlined by us). Therefore, it is ex-facie clear that because of the deliberate supply of the wrong information in the Land Use Certificate Form adverted to above, the Special Project Certificate has stood cancelled automatically too. In this regard as well, no further order of cancellation of the Special Project Certificate is required from RAJUK.

42.         It is worthy of notice that the Rules of 2008 were framed under the Building Construction Act, 1952 and accordingly RAJUK issued sanctions for the impugned construction on the case property and slapped some stipulations both in the Land Use Certificate and the Special Project Certificate as per section 3 of the aforesaid Act of 1952. For intentionally furnishing the wrong information by the respondent nos. 6 and 13 as above, the sanctions granted by RAJUK in respect of the impugned construction on the case property can not be maintained at all pursuant to section 9 of the Act of 1952.

43.         As this is a classic case of perpetration of fraud by the respondent nos. 6 and 13, both the Land Use Certificate and the Special Project Certificate have become non-existent in the eye of law. By the way, we are reminded of an off-quoted legal dictum- “Fraud vitiates everything”. It is well-settled that no party can be allowed to enjoy the fruit of its fraud.

44.         Be that as it may, the respondent nos. 6 and 13 will have to apply to RAJUK afresh for a Land Use Certificate and a Special Project Certificate for the impugned construction on the case property. If those respondents file applications to RAJUK afresh to the above effect, then RAJUK will review the entire gamut of the issues involved and consider their pros and cons and arrive at a correct decision as to granting or non-granting of any Land Use Certificate and Special Project Certificate in the light of the relevant laws.

45.         Since we have confined ourselves to the questions of maintainability of the Writ Petition and perpetration of fraud upon RAJUK in issuing the Land Use Certificate and the Special Project Certificate for the impugned construction, we refrain from making any observations and recording any findings on the submissions of Mr. Junayed Ahmed Chowdhury and the counter-submissions of Mr. Md. Nurul Amin relating to the merit of the Rule.

46.         In view of the foregoing discussions and in the facts and circumstances of the case, the Rule is disposed of without any order as to costs. However, the impugned construction on the case property shall remain stayed pending any decision by RAJUK in the light of the observations made in the body of this judgment.

Ed.


Writ Petition No. 4808 of 2018

719

Ashis Kumar Mahajan Vs. Bangladesh Bar Council & ors., (Kashefa Hussain, J.)

Case No: First Miscellaneous Appeal No. 141 of 2011 With Civil Rule No. 213 (F.M.)of 2011

Judge: S. M. Emdadul Hoque, J And Kashefa Hussain, J

Court: High Court Division,

Advocate: Mr. Subrata Chowdhury with Mr. Sarowar Alam Chowdhury, Mr. Samir Majumder, Mr. Robin Chandra Paul and Mr. Md. Mominul Islam, Advocates,

Citation: 2019(1) LNJ

Case Year: 2017

Appellant: Ashis Kumar Mahajan @ Chowdhury

Respondent: Bangladesh Bar Council and others

Subject: Bangladesh Legal Practitioners and Bar Council Order

Delivery Date: 2019-11-26

HIGH COURT DIVISION

(CIVIL REVISIONAL JURISDICTION)

S. M. Emdadul Hoque, J

And

Kashefa Hussain, J

 

Judgment on

29.10.2017

}

}

}

}

Ashis Kumar Mahajan @ Chowdhury

. . . Appellant

-Versus-

Bangladesh Bar Council and others

. . .Respondents

Bangladesh Legal Practitioners and Bar Council Order (PO 46 of 1972)

Order 33(1)

Order 33(1) of the order of 1972 provides for a tribunal comprising of 3 persons under the Bar Council Order. Whereas in the instant case it is found that only two persons were conducting the proceedings of the tribunal and which is clear as daylight from the signature made in the order. Therefore, the impugned order dated 05.03.2011 passed by the tribunal suffers from the inherent illegality of Coram Non-judice and is not maintainable under the law and ought to be set-aside. However, we do not find it necessary to mull upon the factual issues since the order is inherently defective and unlawful, suffering from the illegality of Coram Non- judice upon violation of the provisions under order 33(1) of the Bangladesh Legal Practitioners and Bar Council Order,1972.    . . . (7)

Mr. Subrata Chowdhury with

Mr. Sarowar Alam Chowdhury,

Mr. Samir Majumder,

Mr. Robin Chandra Paul and

Mr. Md. Mominul Islam, Advocates

. . . For the Appellant

Mr. Muntu Kumar Mondal, Advocate

. . . For the Respondents

JUDGMENT

Kashefa Hussain, J. This appeal is directed against the judgment and order dated 05.03.2011 passed by the Tribunal No. 11, Bangladesh Bar Council in Complaint Case No. 3 of 2003 (22/2002) suspending the appellant-petitioner from practicing as Advocate for 1(one) year.

2.             Facts relevant for disposal of this appeal inter alia is that the case arose between the present appellant and the respondent in this First Miscellaneous Appeal under the circumstances that the present respondent No. 2 as complainant filed a complaint against the present appellant under Complaint Case No. 22 of 2002 subsequently renumbered as Complaint Case No. 3 of 2003 in the Bangladesh Bar Council making several allegations including that of physical assault against the present appellant (opposite party in complainant case No. 03 of 2003) and the complainant opposite party stated that it amounts to professional misconduct of the appellant being opposite party in the complaint case. The appellant (opposite party in Complainant case No. 03 of 2003) submitted written statement denying the allegations made against him. After hearing, an order was passed by the Bangladesh Bar Council Tribunal No. 2 dated 05.03.2011 suspending the appellant from practicing as an Advocate for one year from the date of the said order passed dated 05.03.2011. The said order of the tribunal No. 2 of Bangladesh Bar Council dated 05.03.2011 was passed under the signature of two persons namely Mr. Md. Yahya, Chairman, Tribunal No. 2 Bangladesh Bar Council and Mr. Sheikh Aktarul Islam, member, Bangladesh Bar Council. Being aggrieved by the order dated 05.03.2011 passed by the Bangladesh Bar Council the opposite party in Complaint Case No. 03 of 2003 as Appellant preferred the instant Civil Miscellaneous Appeal which is before us for disposal.

3.             Learned Advocate Mr. Subrata Chowdhury along with Mr. Sarowar Alam Chowdhury appeared for the appellant (opposite party in Complaint Case No. 03 of 2003) while none appeared for the respondents.

4.             However, power has been filed by the learned Advocate Mr. Mintu Kumar Mondol on behalf of the respondent No. 2.

5.             Learned Advocate Mr. Subrata Chowdhury on behalf of the appellant (opposite party in complaint case No. 03 of 2003) opens his submissions upon assertion that the impugned judgment and order dated 05.03.2011 passed by the Tribunal No. 2 Bangladesh Bar Council in Complaint Case No. 3 of 2003 suspending the appellant for one year from practice is illegal, unlawful and not maintainable. He elaborates his contention relying upon his argument that the impugned order suffers from an inherent defect of being Coram non-judice. He contends that under section 33 (1) of the Bangladesh Legal Practitioners and Bar Council Order and Rules, 1972 the number of persons consisting of a Tribunal of the Bangladesh Bar Council shall constitute of 3 persons. He draws our attention to the impugned order dated 05.03.2011 passed in complaint case No. 3 of 2003 and points out that in the instant case the Tribunal most unlawfully passed the order under the signature of two persons only. In the light of his submissions he persists that hence such an order has flouted and violated the prescribed Rules provided in section 33 (1) of the Bangladesh Legal Practitioners and Bar Council Order and Rules, 1972 and thus is inherently an unlawful order and not maintainable. Mr. Subrata Chowdhury also makes some submissions relying upon some alleged facts relating to the allegations made against the appellant including the allegations of physical assault and the learned Advocate submits that all these allegations made against him are false. He concludes his submissions upon assertion that under the facts and circumstances and in the light of the provisions of Section 33 (1) of the Bangladesh Legal practitioners and Bar Council Order and Rules, 1972  the impugned Order dated 05.03.2011 suffering from an inherent defect of being Coram Non-judice and the allegations being wrong, therefore, the order of suspension dated 05.03.2011 from one year of practice ought to be set aside and the appeal be allowed and the connected Rule be made absolute for ends of justice.

6.             We have heard the learned Advocate for the appellant and we have perused the materials and the records before us including the impugned order passed by the Tribunal No. 2 Bangladesh Bar Council dated 05.03.2011. From the impugned order it is clear that the order was passed under the signature of 2 persons. We have perused the provisions of section 33 (1) of the Bangladesh Legal Practitioners and Bar Council Order and Rules, 1972 which reads:

   The Bar Council may constitute one or more Tribunals and each such Tribunal shall consist of three persons of whom two shall be persons elected by the council from amongst its members and the other shall be a person co-opted by the Council from amongst the advocates on the roll, and the senior most advocate amongst the members of a Tribunal shall be its chairman.

7.             Needless to say that it is evident that upon scrutiny of the impugned order and upon perusal of section 33 (1) of Bangladesh Legal Practitioners and Bar Council Order and Rules, 1972, it is crystal clear that the tribunal did not follow the provisions of the Bar Council Order of 1972. Section 33(1) of the order of 1972 provides for a tribunal comprising of 3 persons under the Bar Council Order. Whereas in the instant case it is found that only two persons were conducting the proceedings of the tribunal and which is clear as daylight from the signature made in the order. Therefore, the impugned order dated 05.03.2011 passed by the tribunal suffers from the inherent illegality of Coram Non-judice and is not maintainable under the law and ought to be set-aside. Senior Advocate Mr. Subrata Chowdhury in his submissions also raised some factual issues denying the several allegations including the allegations of physical assault made against the appellant. However, we do not find it necessary to mull upon these factual issues since the order is inherently defective and unlawful, suffering from the illegality of Coram Non-judice upon violation of the provisions under section 33 (1) of the Bangladesh Legal Practitioners and Bar Council Order and Rules, 1972.

8.             In the light of the submissions made by the learned Advocate for the appellant and upon perusal of the documents and the impugned order and upon examination of the relevant Rules we are inclined to allowed the instant First Miscellaneous appeal.

Babu @ Md. Robiul Islam Babu Vs. Amjad Ali & ors., (Soumendra Sarker, J.)

Subject: Specific Relief Act

Babu @ Md. Robiul Islam Babu

. . . Defendant No. 01-Petitioner

-Versus-

Amjad Ali and others

. . .Plaintiff-Opposite parties

Specific Relief Act (I of 1877)

Section 9

No Appeal lies against the judgment and decree of a suit filed under section 9 of the S.R Act, but only Civil Revision lies before the High Court Division—The Law enjoins that the appeal against the judgment and decree of a suit under section 9 of the Specific Relief Act, 1877 is not maintainable, as we as against the judgment of the Appellate Court the Civil Revision is also not maintainable and the proper forum is filing of the Civil Revision in the High Court Division against the judgment and decree of a suit filed under section 9 of the Specific Relief Act, 1877. But here in this case, the engaged lawyer of the Applicant instead of proper forum of law, in wrong forum filed one after another case up to the Honorable Appellate Division having no fruitful result.  . . . (9)

Limitation Act (IX of 1908)

Section 5

Lawyer’s wrong advice constitutes sufficient cause to condone the inordinate delay-Section 5 of the Limitation Act, 1908 provides that in appropriate case the condonation of delay can be done. Lawyer’s wrong advice may be a good ground for condoning the delay. Mistaken advice given by the legal practitioner may in the circumstances of a particular case give rise to sufficient cause within the section though there is certainly no general doctrine, which saves the parties from the result of wrong advice. Under the meaning of this section “sufficient cause” is something beyond the control of the party. In this instant case obviously, it is noticed that the Defendant No. 1- Petitioner had no negligence or laches but for the wrong advice of his lawyer he went up to the Honorable Appellate Division. Consequently, the inordinate delay of 2196 days occurred and it was in the good faith of the Applicant and the delay caused due to the lack of jurisdiction of the Court. the entire circumstances of this case led me to hold such a view that the delay caused for filing of the revisional application although inordinate, but it is not for the laches or the negligence of the Applicant, rather; it was due to wrong bona fide advice/instruction of the lawyer concerned. Hence, this Rule has got much merit to succeed.         ...(11, 12, 15 and 16)

Limitation Act (IX of 1908)

Section 14

In computing the period of limitation prescribed for any suit, the time during which the plaintiff has been prosecuting with due diligence another civil proceeding, whether in a Court of first instance or in a Court of appeal, against the defendant, shall be excluded, where the proceeding is founded upon the same cause of action and is prosecuted in good faith in a Court which, from defect of jurisdiction, or other cause of a like nature, is unable to entertain it.  . . . (13)

Nitya Gopal Saha Vs. Binod Behari Saha 29 DLR 259 and Managing Director, Rupali Bank Ltd. Vs. Haji Jahanar Begum being dead her heirs: 1(A) Haji Arab Ali and others ref.

Mr. Subrata Saha, with

Mr. Zainul Abedin, Advocates

. . .For the petitioner

Mr. Ekramul Islam, with

Mr. Rafiqul Islam Sarder, Advocates

. . . For the Opposite parties.

                        JUDGMENT

Soumendra Sarker, J: The Rule issued calling upon the Opposite parties No.01-05 to show cause as to why the delay of 2196 days in preferring the revisional application against the judgment and decree dated 06.09.2009 passed by the learned Senior Assistant Judge, 8th Court, Dhaka in Title Suit No. 82 of 2007 should not be condoned and/or pass such other order or further order or orders as to this Court may seem fit and proper.

2.             The facts giving rise to the issuance of the Rule in a nutshell can be stated as follows: The present Opposite parties as Plaintiffs instituted the Title Suit being No. 82 of 2007 in the Court of learned Senior Assistant Judge, Dohar, Dhaka against the Defendant-Petitioner and others. The trial court after trial decreed the suit on 06.09.2009. Being aggrieved the Defendant No. 01 as Appellant preferred a Title Appeal being No. 412 of 2009 in the Court of learned District Judge, Dhaka which was transmitted to the 3rd Court of learned Additional District Judge, Dhaka and the learned Additional District Judge by his judgment and decree dated 14.11.2013 disallowed the appeal and affirmed the judgment and decree passed by the trial court.

3.             Being aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the judgment and decree of the Appellate Court the Defendant No. 01 filed a Civil Revision No. 275 of 2014 before this court. Thereafter, this court by its judgment and order dated 26.05.2015 discharged the Rule. Against that judgment and order the Defendant No. 01 filed a Civil Miscellaneous Petition No. 577 of 2015 before the Honorable Appellate Division. Subsequently, in the Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 2778 of 2015 that was dismissed having no merit. Thereafter, realizing the mistake, in the proper forum against the judgment and decree of the Trial Court, the present Applicant-Defendant No. 01 against whom the decree of recovery of khas possession was passed, has preferred a Civil Revision in this court under section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure, but in filing of the said Civil Revision, there has been a delay of 2196 days. For condonation of the said delay, the Defendant No. 01-Petitioner as has Applicant filed the instant application under section 5 read with section 14 of the Limitation Act, 1908.

4.             During hearing of the Rule, the learned Advocate Mr. Zainul Abedin appeared on behalf of the Applicant while Mr. Md. Ekramul Islam and Mr. Rafiqul Islam Sarder appeared on behalf of the Opposite parties.

5.             The learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the Applicant submits that, due to unavoidable circumstances the delay occurred which was unintentional and not for the latches of the Defendant No. 01-Applicant. The learned Advocate further submits that, the trial court after taking evidence from the sides of the parties passed its judgment and decree on 06.09.2009 directing the Defendant No. 01 to vacate the house, which is the suit property, within 60 days. Thereafter, the Defendant No. 01 against the said decree preferred a Title Appeal No. 412 of 2009 before the learned District Judge, Dhaka. That appeal was disposed of by the learned Additional District Judge, 3rd Court, Dhaka on 14.11.2013 dismissing the same. Being aggrieved the Defendant No. 01 filed a Civil Revision No. 275 of 2014 before this court and obtained a Rule with an interim order of staying further proceedings of Execution Case No. 03 of 2009 pending in the Court of learned Assistant Judge, Dohar, Dhaka. In that Civil Revision the Rule was discharged on 26.05.2015. The learned Advocate also submits that, the Defendant-Applicant against the order of the High Court Division filed a Civil Miscellaneous Petition  No. 577 of 2015 before the Honorable Appellate Division and obtained an order of stay of further proceedings of the Execution Case. Subsequently, the Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 2778 of 2015 was dismissed on 09.12.2015. The learned Advocate lastly submits that the Defendant-Petitioner-Applicant on good faith was fully dependant on his lawyer, who; due to wrong impression filed the cases one after another in wrong forum causing inordinate delay in institution of the Civil Revision before the proper court. The Defendant was very much diligent and sincere for redress of his grievances. In this context, the learned Advocate referred some decision of this court and our Apex Court.

6.             Vis-à-vis, the learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the Opposite parties opposing Rule and submission advanced from the side of the learned Advocate for the Petitioner-Applicant submits that, there is no reasonable cause which can be treated sufficient for condonation of delay, but the Defendant-Petitioner-Applicant only to harass the Plaintiff-Opposite parties has filed the application for condonation of delay, which is liable to be rejected.

7.             In order to appreciate the submission advanced from the sides of the learned counsels of the parties, having gone through the relevant papers, I find that the present Opposite parties being Plaintiffs filed the Original Title Suit No. 82 of 2007 on 28.11.2007 under section 09 of the Specific Relief Act, 1877. That suit was decreed against the present Applicant on 06.09.2009. It also appears from the relevant papers that the Title Suit No. 82 of 2007 was a suit for recovery of khas possession and the decree was passed against the Defendant No. 01 directing him to hand over vacant possession of the suit premises in favour of the Plaintiff-Opposite parties. It also transpires from the connected papers that the Defendant No. 01 as Appellant preferred a Title Appeal No. 412 of 2009 before the learned District Judge, Dhaka which was transmitted to the 3rd Court of the learned Additional District Judge, Dhaka for hearing and disposal, and the learned Additional District Judge vide judgment and order dated 14.11.2013 affirmed the judgment and decree of the Trial Court. Thereafter, against that decree a Civil Revision No. 275 of 2014 was filed before this High Court Division. Ultimately, the Rule which was issued in that Civil Revision was discharged on 26.05.2015.

8.             It is apparent from the face of the linked papers that the learned lawyer who was engaged on behalf of the Petitioner after the disposal of the Civil Revision filed a Civil Miscellaneous Petition being No. 577 of 2015 before the Honorable Appellate Division of the Supreme Court of Bangladesh against the judgment and order of the High Court Division. Ultimately, the Honorable Appellate Division in the Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 2778 of 2015 dismissed the same uttering the word “no merit” on 09.12.2015.

9.             The law enjoins that the appeal against the judgment and decree of a suit under section 09 of the Specific Relief Act, 1877[I of 1877] is not maintainable, as well as against the judgment of the Appellate Court the Civil Revision is also not maintainable and the proper forum is filing of the Civil Revision in the High Court Division against the judgment and decree of a suit filed under section 09 of the Specific Relief Act, 1877[I of 1877]. But here in this case, the engaged lawyer of the Applicant instead of proper forum of law, in wrong forum filed one after another case up to the Honorable Appellate Division having no fruitful result. 

10.         It also appears from the relevant papers that after the disposal of the Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 2778 of 2015, the Defendant-Petitioner has come to this court for filing of the Civil Revision, but meanwhile an inordinate delay of 2196 days occurred.

11.         Section 05 of the Limitation Act, 1908 provides that in appropriate case the condonation of delay can be done. In the case of Nitya Gopal Saha vs Binod Behari Saha 29 DLR 259 this Court held that the delay due to wrong but bona fide advice of the lawyer is a sufficient explanation of delay. Lawyer’s wrong advice may be a good ground for condoning the delay. Mistaken advice given by the legal practitioner may in the circumstances of a particular case give rise to sufficient cause within the section though there is certainly no general doctrine, which saves the parties from the result of wrong advice.

12.         Under the meaning of this section “sufficient cause” is something beyond the control of the party. In this instant case obviously, it is noticed that the Defendant No. 01-Petitioner had no negligence or latches but for the wrong advice of his lawyer he went up to the Honorable Appellate Division. Consequently, the inordinate delay of 2196 days occurred and it was in the good faith of the Applicant and the delay caused due to the lack of jurisdiction of the court.

13.         Section 14 of the Limitation Act, 1908 contemplates: Exclusion of time of proceedings bona fide in court without jurisdiction- in computing the period of limitation prescribed for any suit, the time during which the plaintiff has been prosecuting with due diligence another civil proceeding, whether in a Court of first instance or in a Court of appeal, against the defendant, shall be excluded, where the proceeding is founded upon the same cause of action and is prosecuted in good faith in a Court which, from defect of jurisdiction, or other cause of a like nature, is unable to entertain it.

14.         This bench in the case of Managing Director, Rupali Bank Ltd. vs. Haji Jahanara Begum being dead her heirs : 1(A) Haji Arab Ali and others held that the delay caused, if beyond the control of the applicant and there is nothing to hold such a view and draw such inference that the applicant was negligent and was dormant in getting the relief as sought for in wrong forum, the delay needs to be condoned to meet up justice, inasmuch as; the delay occurred purely due to the wrong but bona fide advice of the lawyer, engaged in conducting the case.

15.         Under the above facts and circumstances of this case, the entire circumstances of this case led me to hold such a view that the delay caused for filing of the revisional application although inordinate, but it is not for the latches or the negligence of the Applicant, rather; it was due to wrong bona fide advice/ instruction of the lawyer concerned.

16.         Hence, this Rule has got much merit to succeed.

17.         In the result, the Rule is made absolute without any order as to costs. The delay of 2196 days in preferring the revisional application is hereby condoned.

18.          Office is directed to do the needful at once.

Ed.


Civil Revision No. 4269(con) of 2015

721

Bangladesh and others Vs. Md. Abdus Satter and others, (Surendra Kumar Sinha, CJ.)

Case No: CIVIL APPEAL No.73 OF 2012

Nazmun Ara Sultana, J
